Round 1: Feature Match – Ari Lax vs. David Sharfman
---------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

Here in the hallowed halls of the Indianapolis Convention Center, which I say in all seriousness, a great event is taking place. Gen Con, the best four days in gaming have drawn thousands of people together to share their love of gaming. One of the marquee events this year, at least as far as readers of this piece are concerned, is U.S. Nationals. The best players in the United States have come to vie for the chance to represent 'Murrica at Worlds on their home turf, in San Francisco, later this year.


### Game One


The first round started with a bang, giving us a great matchup between Ari Lax, who has been around the block a fair number of times, with some recent Top 8s at GP Nashville in 2010 and Atlanta earlier this year. His opponent is David Sharfman, who has just *cruised* this year, winning GP Paris and PT Nagoya earlier this year.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm1%20Lax.jpg)*Ari Lax*
Sharfman started things off with a mulligan, his deck showing him a weak opening hand. Lax started off with an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island), something which was probably going to be a popular first-turn play over the course of the day. Sharfman gave me pause for a moment when he played a [Verdant Catacombs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Verdant+Catacombs), fetching a forest to play a [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise). The next few turns were spent building mana, both players avoiding any more commintments to the board. When Sharfman broke the stalemate at the end of Lax's turn for a [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch), the pieces all came together in my head. Lax had a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak), but it put opened the window. The [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) that followed from Sharfman immediately upgraded the Birds to a [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite), to protect him from a Twin combo from Lax. Considering Lax hadn't played a non-land permanent, and the [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) he had in play, it seemed a good bet that he was playing the UR version of the [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) combo deck.


Sharfman started to use his Pod to great effect over the next turns, playing a [Sylvan Ranger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Ranger) which turned into a [Sea Gate Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sea+Gate+Oracle).


"Value," he exclaimed!


Lax made a [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) on the end of Sharfman's turn, but didn't really have anything to do with it over the next couple of turns. He [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) ed and [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) ed to dig for a way to get himself ahead, but other than that did nothing. Sharfman, meanwhile, kept Podding. Oracle turned into [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph), and he played a [Sylvok Replica](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvok+Replica) as well. Between the Replica and his [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite), he looked to be in complete control. An [Acidic Slime](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Acidic+Slime) on the next turn ate Lax's [Shrine of Piercing Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Piercing+Vision) before getting upgraded into a [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan). This massive, and rapidly upgrading army, was facing down a lone [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch). Even it went away as Lax was forced to chump block the rampaging Titan on the following turn. When Sharfman used his Pod to make his Replica into an [Entomber Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomber+Exarch), which prompted Lax to concede rather than reveal his hand.


**Ari Lax 0 – David Sharfman 1**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm1%20Sharfman.jpg)*David Sharfman*
### Game Two


Lax started the second game digging through his deck with a couple of [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain)s, which is quickly becoming a hallmark of his games. Intermixed with those, he resolved a free [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe), revealing a [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum), [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan), [Memoricide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Memoricide), and [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim). When Sharfman tried for the [Memoricide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Memoricide), a [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) stopped it cold. Lax made a [Shrine of Piercing Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shrine+of+Piercing+Vision), leaving one mana up and giving Sharfman a temporary reprieve. He made a [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) and used a [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) to end the Shrine, which Lax simply replaced. Sharfman punished Lax's weak draw on the following turn with a [Frost Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frost+Titan), which sealed the match after a couple of attacks.


**Ari Lax 0 – David Sharfman 2**




Round 2: Feature Match – Paul Rietzl vs. Alex West
--------------------------------------------------


*by Brian David-Marshall* 

"Morning, gentlemen," I said cheerfully as the two competitors sat down for the second round of the tournament but I was still looking down and getting the camera ready and opening up a blank document and did not see the glum look on either of their faces.


"You realize that we both lost, right?" sighed Rietzl.


Both players came into this event with their eyes no doubt on picking up some of the precious Pro Points available at Nationals. With his Finals finish in Paris — and double tabling of Grand Prix Paris at the same time -- Rietzl is within the Top 10 of the Player of the Year race. Additionally with 10 days left for members of the two Pro Tour Hall of Fame committees to submit — or even resubmit — their ballots a National team berth might be the **Magic** equivalent of shaking hands and kissing babies.


For Alex the Pro Points are even more important. The Star City Games columnist has not even gotten on the board for the Player of the Year race — the only players listed on the page have 10 or more points so far this season — getting the minimum point payout at each of the first two Pro Tours so far this season.


When you lose round one of an event like Nationals the hope is that you will get paired with a relatively inexperienced player in the 0-1 bracket and will be able to get back on track. As they walked to the pairings board the last name they wanted to see across from their was one they recognized.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm2%20Rietzl.jpg)*Paul Rietzl*
"Should I have said 'Mourning gentlemen.'"


"I haven't won a Constructed match at Nationals since 1999," Rietzl said wryly.


"Some would say the odds are in your favor," offered Alex who rolled very low on his dice. "You are a favorite to win this die roll..."


"Tied it," slumped Rietzl who would eventually win the reroll.


### Game One


Rietzl led off with [Porcelain Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Porcelain+Legionnaire) off of a [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) and [Inkmoth Nexus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inkmoth+Nexus) — he was playing [Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempered+Steel). Alex played [Spreading Seas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spreading+Seas) on his [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) rather than his [Inkmoth Nexus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inkmoth+Nexus) out of respect for the eponymous enchantment. Rietzl added [Vault Skirge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vault+Skirge) to his team as well as [Glint Hawk Idol](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glint+Hawk+Idol). West played Colonnade and passed the turn.


Rietzl offered up another Idol but it was [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) ed. Rietzl paid to animate the one from the previous turn and attacked for 6. Day of Judgement from West cleared away most of the threats but Rietzl was able to animate both Idol and Nexus and swing in for 2 and 1 before playing another Nexus.


West's deck was starting to rumble to life as he played an [Everflowing Chalice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Everflowing+Chalice) for 1 and [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) ed the Idol. Rietzl sighed and went to his back up plan, animating both of the Inkmoths and scratching away. West paid full price for [Tezzeret's Gambit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tezzeret%27s+Gambit) and nudged up his Chalice to two counters. Rietzl had [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite). He was tight on mana and could only get in for 1 poison counter that turn.


Rietzl played a second Chalice for 1 and then summoned [Consecrated Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consecrated+Sphinx). Rietzl frowned at the board but he had a plan. He animated both his Nexi during his upkeep and [Dispatch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispatch) ed the Sphinx before drawing a card. He snuck in for another point of poison. West slowed the infection with [Spreading Seas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spreading+Seas) on one of the two Nexi. He played another Gambit for full price and forged another Chalice.


Rietzl attempted to land [Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempered+Steel) bit it was met with [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak). His Nexus got in for the 6th poison counter. West tapped an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) and a Chalice with three counters on it to Gambit again. He left Colonnade mana up and ORinged the [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) but he had to [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) another [Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempered+Steel) on Rietzl's turn. Rietzl was able to get 7th or a 7th poison but — with just a little sweat starting to show on his brow — West finally found a [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge). He attacked with two Colonnades and passed.


Rietzl finally landed a [Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempered+Steel) and followed it with [Vault Skirge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vault+Skirge) and [Signal Pest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Signal+Pest). West killed the Inkmoth EOT and untapped to kill everything else with Day of Judgement. He played yet another [Tezzeret's Gambit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tezzeret%27s+Gambit) and had his Chalices at 5,4, and 3. [Baneslayer Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Baneslayer+Angel) was enough for Rietzl to slide the pair of Seas across the table and wrinkled up his face in disgust as he reached for the sideboard.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm2%20West.jpg)*Alex West*
### Game Two


[Glint Hawk Idol](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glint+Hawk+Idol) led off for Rietzl and West's [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) on [Steel Overseer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Overseer) saved two points of damage with no third land for the Pro Tour Amsterdam champion. West played a pair of Chalices over the next two turns and then went to 16 to pay the Phyrexian mana cost for Gambit and boost them both up with Proliferate in between Rietzl playing [Memnite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Memnite) and [Signal Pest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Signal+Pest).


Rietzl was able to attack for 5 but was still scuffling for mana. Meanwhile, West had all the mana in the world and played [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) into [Baneslayer Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Baneslayer+Angel). He O-Ringed the Idol and then played Angel. Rietzl who had sided out all but one of his [Dispatch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispatch) es shrugged and said okay as he played [Signal Pest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Signal+Pest).


West attacked for nine and then Spread a [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains) and [Oust](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oust) ed a [Signal Pest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Signal+Pest). Rietzl nodded and started to fill out the result slip.


**Final result: Alex West - 2 Paul Rietzl - 0**


"I don't really like the new versions of CawBlade," said West after the match wen asked about his decision to play a blue-white control deck. "Once you are paying full price for Swords I would rather be paying that price on better guys. Everyone keeps teasing me that it is the control deck of a small child. Last round I cast a turn 5 Karn with [Cancel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cancel) backup."




Round 3: How Can You Beat That Which Does Not Kill? – Kyle Sanchez vs. Orrin Beasley
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro* 

"Yo, you a net-decker?" Kyle Sanchez snarked at his opponent. He may have been away from **Magic** for a while, but he still knew how to toy with an opponent.


"Maybe," a meeker Orrin Beasley replied.


"I tell ya, man, there's no pride in **Magic** anymore." Kyle shook his head disdainfully and shuffled his cards. His unique mill deck had been taking down some unlikely contenders so far, and we'll see how it fairs against Beasley's CawBlade. Sanchez said in his testing with Pro Tour—Hollywood winner Charles Gindy, this match was 80% in his favor. 80% seems pretty darn good. Those are close to Owling Mine numbers, I think.


But it's time for Kyle Sanchez to put his money where his mouth is.


### Game One



![Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Preordain)

Sanchez started off with an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) into a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), yielding a nice turn-two [Lotus Cobra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Cobra) and a turn-three pre-fetchland [Hedron Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hedron+Crab). However, the Crab was promptly [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) ed by Beasley, who spent his own first turns [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) ing and keeping mana up for said counterspell things. [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring), [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk), [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment), [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) and a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) lay waiting in Beasley's hand.


Turn four Sanchez had up 2 [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s, a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) and a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain), and thanks to [Lotus Cobra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Cobra), cast [Archive Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archive+Trap) on his opponent.


"A couple Swords and a Hawk. Not bad." Kyle mused.


Beasley's [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk) in-hand came down and searched two buddies, then Beasley laid the Horror artifact creature.


Sanchez cycled a Visions from Beyond (rather than Ancestral Recalling with it), revealing his desperation, then laid a [Jace, Memory Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+Memory+Adept), drew a card while casting a free Glimpse the Unthinkable, then shipped his turn. [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) came down, equipped, then aided Beasley's attack to make the totals 17-16 in Sanchez's favor. Post-combat, Beasley O-Ring'ed away the opposing Planeswalker. Sanchez had some tricks to foil the Sworded-up bird, but totals still became 9-14. And single digits was not good for Sanchez and his milling compatriots.


Facing lethal next turn, as more birds and more Swords cluttered Beasley's side, Sanchez drew, sighed, and scooped up his cards.


**Orrin Beasley 1 – 0 Kyle Sanchez**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm3%20Beasley.jpg)*Orrin Beasley*
### Game Two


Dueling [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain)s, and Sanchez followed with a [Hedron Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hedron+Crab) and a [Terramorphic Expanse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terramorphic+Expanse). Beasley simply held up [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) mana, and caught a second Crab, then swept the O-G Original Crab with an O-B [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring).



![Jace, Memory Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Jace%2C+Memory+Adept)

*A turn or two passed before Kyle cast [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil) at the end of Beasley's turn to get his [Hedron Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hedron+Crab) back in time to have two uncracked fetchlands (an [Scalding Tarn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scalding+Tarn) and a [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) ) in play. After some cracking and some fetching, Beasley got his turn back with 21 cards in his graveyard. He calmly tapped out for a [Gideon Jura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gideon+Jura), and was caught in an [Archive Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archive+Trap) at the end of his turn. He had 5 cards in his hand, and only 15 cards left in his library.*


Two Visions from Beyond restocked Sanchez's hand (this time they Recalled), allowing Sanchez to cast [Explore](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explore), play a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) and a [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) (milling for nine in the process), then two [Lotus Cobra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Cobra)s and a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain). He bottomed two lands, drew an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island), and passed the turn with a [Jace, Memory Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+Memory+Adept) and a third [Lotus Cobra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Cobra) alongside the unwanted blue land.


Gideon was lonely. Sanchez was still at 17 life, and Beasley's library was low. Very low. Jura did what he could. He grabbed a [Sword of Feast and Famine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Feast+and+Famine) and took Sanchez to single digits, but Sanchez's Jace was more than willing to take Beasley's remaining cards and throw them in the trash.


**Orrin Beasley 1 – 1 Kyle Sanchez**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm3%20Sanchez.jpg)*Kyle Sanchez*
### Game Three


These early cyclers are getting a bit predictable, but thankfully, Sanchez fought Beasley's [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) with a turn-one [Hedron Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hedron+Crab), and Beasley decided a [Squadron Hawk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Squadron+Hawk), searching up for two friends, was a better second-turn play than holding up [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) mana. The library searching allowed Sanchez to [Archive Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archive+Trap) for free. This was important because after a [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), Sanchez's hand was merely four lands and another [Archive Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archive+Trap). If his [Hedron Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hedron+Crab) bit the dust, he might have some trouble on his hands.


It was about to do just that to a [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) the following turn, but Sanchez had drawn an [Into the Roil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Into+the+Roil), like a curly-haired boss, to save it. Beasley's board was three Hawks, and he was able to [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) Kyle's re-cast [Hedron Crab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hedron+Crab). Sanchez was ok with that though; he had another one sitting in his hand, again, like the aforementioned boss.


Sanchez knew how to play this deck. Every time I got up to count the cards in Beasley's graveyard, he would say the number immediately when I put the deck down.


"25?" he asked. I nodded.


Sanchez's various [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain)s and [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder)s found him more Crabs. One was [Oblivion Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oblivion+Ring) -ed while a [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) joined the 1/1 Hawks. Sanchez sunk to 9, milled his opponent with his remaining Crab, then cracked fetchlands to mill some more.



![Archive Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Archive+Trap)

"You should have 10 cards in your library?"


"11."


"Ok. Hm. How many [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce)s are in your 'yard?" He silently counted them up. It was clear Sanchez had a plan.


"On your upkeep, [Archive Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archive+Trap) ?" Ah yes, *that* plan.


Beasley thought for a moment, then scooped up his cards. It looks like that 80% win rate might not be too skewed after all.


**Kyle Sanchez 2 – 1 Orrin Beasley**


Kyle Sanchez's deck has some really neat tricks up its sleeve, and some that he requested I not reveal this early in the tournament. Stay turned for more on this surprising little deck.




Friday, 1:30 p.m. – A Quick Look at Vintage
-------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

Ah Vintage, the least understood of **Magic**'s many formats (Chaos Planechase Archenemy Emperor Commander notwithstanding). Vintage has been around for actual ever, but very few people outside of the dedicated community seem to show any interest in it. As the years have passed, players have started to become more and more interested in the older formats. All you have to do is look at the booming popularity of Legacy to see that that is true. Many players have looked down on Vintage as a stagnant, never-changing format filled with broken cards, non-interactive matches, and generally not worth their time to get into.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vintageCards.jpg)Honestly, it's a shame. After years of covering the Vintage Championhips, I've learned how wrong those opinions are. The format is constantly shifting as new cards are added to the mix. Sure, not all of them will be even playable, but every so often, a new superstar comes in and makes waves in the pool, often one you never see coming. The cards are definitely incredibly powerful, but they lend themselves to layers of strategy that don't exist in the other formats. You may think that the Storm mirror match is just going to be a vomit-fest, where someone just dies on the first or second turn with no chance for their opponent to even play **Magic**, but the matchup is actually highly interactive, with a great deal of ebb and flow, and packed with strategic thinking. It really is a rich format, as its very tight community can tell you, and it's only a matter of time before players start to come around. After all, the negative opinions that players have held about the format are eerie echoes of their problems with Legacy, and we can all see how that turned out.


So for those of you that have read this far, and would like to learn more about this very interesting format, let's begin by taking a look at what comes together to make Vintage. One of the biggest hallmarks of Vintage is the presence of the powerful older cards. Cards of legend, like the [Moxen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?action=advanced&name=+%5Bmox%5D&set=%7C%5B%22Limited%20Edition%20Alpha%22%5D), [Black Lotus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Lotus), [Ancestral Recall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Recall), [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk), [Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop) …these are definitely the first things that jump to peoples' minds when you think of Vintage, and with good reason. They are some of the most powerful cards ever printed, and that definitely contributes to the power level of the format as a whole. Up next is an interesting phenomenon that occurs in Vintage and Legacy to a lesser extent. Because of the sheer size of the card pool, there are often cards that will have a very big impact in Vintage that are virtually unplayable in other formats. One of the best examples of this is the card [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/slashPanther.jpg)All right, believe me when I say that the first time I heard about this, I just started to laugh, assuming that someone was playing a joke on me. But as they explained it, it really started to make sense. While a player might get mocked mercilessly out of the room were they to play [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) in Standard right now, it fills many important roles in Vintage.



![Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Phyrexian+Metamorph)

*The deck it has found a home in is the [Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop) -based artifact decks that are major players in the Vintage scene. The deck used to run [Juggernaut](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Juggernaut) as a kill condition, since a first-turn 5-powered creature tends to end things in short order. Back that up with some disruption in the form of [Sphere of Resistance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphere+of+Resistance), [Thorn of Amethyst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thorn+of+Amethyst), and [Tangle Wire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tangle+Wire) and an opponent frequently finds themselves in a world of hurt. When [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem) was released, the deck got a significant upgrade. After all, what is better than disruption and a fat creature? Disruption on a fat creature.*


[Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) is the newest addition to the deck. While a little smaller than its predecessors, it makes up for that in speed. Combined with [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph), which is also proving to be a standout across multiple formats, the hasty Panthers are able to do many things that their cousins could not. For example, they kill [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) immediately (yes, he's even ridiculously good in Vintage). Second, he can actually kill faster than the other two since most players tend to take a little self-inflicted damage in the early turns of the game. All in all, he's just a great versatile addition to the deck. Not exactly the power-level you'd expect from a standout in Vintage, I bet.



![Mystic Remora](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mystic+Remora)

One of the other cool things about Vintage is the fact that there are so many cards that no one can play in other formats because they are too old. These cards only see play in Vintage, and they are just really cool to see in action. [Mystic Remora](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mystic+Remora) is a good example. This simple little enchantment, while it might be nothing more than average or good were it playable in other formats, is an absolute stud in Vintage. You know those Moxes that seem to be running about? They're spells. How about those other cheap spells that seem to be running about, like [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder), [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress), [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain), [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), [Ancestral Recall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Recall), [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will)... I could go on. This card will often draw you an incredible number of cards for an entirely negligible cost. Pretty sexy!


Right now, taking a look around the Vintage world, the format appears to be pretty open. You are going to see variations on decks running [Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop). Some will run the aggressive plan described above, some with [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) and some without. You will also see versions running a control strategy, using [Smokestack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smokestack) to keep opponents locked out of the game. There will be a slew of blue-based control decks. Most will be UB, dipping in to find [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), Tutors, and discard. Often you'll see them playing [Tezzeret the Seeker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tezzeret+the+Seeker) to abuse with their plethora of artifacts and mana-producers. They will all have [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). These decks can really go a number of ways, though setting up a lock with [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault) and either Tezzeret or [Voltaic Key](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voltaic+Key) seems to be the most popular. There will definitely be combo decks in the field as well, with the most popular being the storm decks, killing with either [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony) or [Empty the Warrens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Empty+the+Warrens), and generating their storm count through either Rituals or [Hurkyl's Recall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hurkyl%27s+Recall).



![Kataki, War's Wage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kataki%2C+War%27s+Wage)

There are definitely aggressive decks in the format as well. One of the more popular versions is a BWG "Hate-Bears" deck. It uses the large number of cheap creatures with embedded abilities that happen to be good against these other strategies to hamper them as they smash their faces in. I'm talking [Phyrexian Revoker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Revoker), [Leonin Relic-Warder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leonin+Relic-Warder), [Ethersworn Canonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ethersworn+Canonist), [Aven Mindcensor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Mindcensor), and [Kataki, War's Wage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kataki%2C+War%27s+Wage). These cards lock down a specific element of the opponent's strategy, all the while turning sideways and bringing the game closer to an end. There are the "Fish" variants that run about as well. These run a similar strategy, using cards like [Gaddock Teeg](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaddock+Teeg), [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator), and [Qasali Pridemage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Qasali+Pridemage) to keep people hemmed down, though they reinforce their little men with a suite of countermagic. On top of that, they often keep their hands stocked through [Cold-Eyed Selkie](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cold-Eyed+Selkie), which is a virtually guaranteed card every turn in this heavy-blue field.


Other than that, there are the occasional other decks that have made an appearance. People will still play [Dredge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?action=advanced&text=+%5Bdredge%5D) in every format that the cards are in. They will continue to find ways to cheat creatures into play, either via [Oath of Druids](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Oath+of+Druids), [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) (sometimes both in the same deck), [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker), or reanimator spells. They will play [Painter's Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Painter%27s+Servant) and [Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone) to mill a deck out, or maybe even [Helm of Obedience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Helm+of+Obedience) if they're feeling really old-school. These are all things that have been around Vintage at one time or another, though their power level in the current format is up for debate. Regardless of how strong they are, they are still decks that you have to be aware exist if you hope to play Vintage.


Over the rest of the day, I'll be stopping in with some of the players playing some of the more interesting decks in the field, as well as trying to get some insights into the more consistently performing decks. After all, this format is far deeper than most people give it credit for being, and I'd really like to illustrate how that is so.




Friday, 1:40 p.m. – Day Zero Standard Grinder Winners
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro* 

So I know you guys all want this stuff. You know, the winning Standard decklists that got unqualified players qualified for Nationals? Well guess what, I got 'em right here. No big surprises, but Mono Red lists always make me smile. Watch out for a few interesting cards though. There's an [Abyssal Persecutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abyssal+Persecutor) hidden amongst these cards, and a few [Gravitational Shift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravitational+Shift) s to boot. Additionally, [Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyromancer+Ascension) rears its head to remind us of the other Blue-Red combo deck running around.


These guys showed up ready to enjoy the GenCon weekend, and ended up playing in the big show. Pretty sweet, folks.







#### Alex Bertoncini

3
[Jace Beleren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BJace%5D+%5BBeleren%5D)


4
[Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMana%5D+%5BLeak%5D)

[Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BPreordain%5D)


3
[Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSpell%5D+%5BPierce%5D)

Round 4: Feature Match – Patrick Chapin vs. Dan Jordan
------------------------------------------------------


*by Brian David-Marshall* 

Patrick Chapin needs little in the way of introduction and, after nabbing the fourth career PT Top 8 earlier this year in Paris, could be on his way to getting introduced at Worlds as a member of the incoming Hall of Fame class. With two weeks left for ballots to be turned in, a National team berth would be a nifty bit of last minute resume padding.



![Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Inferno+Titan)

He came prepared for the Standard portion of that feat with a RUG [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) deck designed by him and two-time National team member Michael Jacob. The deck eschewed the [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) combo that has become popular in the wake of results from Australian Nationals and plays more spells and -- more importantly -- more [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan)s.


Dan Jordan is a relatively new player to high-level competition but has been very successful in that short span. He ground his way onto the Pro Tour last season winning a MTGO qualifier for Amsterdam, where he finished in the Top 16. On the Star City Open Series, the Albany native has racked up three victories. He came to the table with a Twin Pod list inspired by [Australian National Champion Aaron Nicoll's winning list](/en/events/coverage/nicoll-nails-it). In preparing for this event Jordan talked with Nicoll and the pair did some fine tuning for this weekend.


### Game One


[Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) kicked off the action for Jordan. "I'll go to nineteen" announced Chapin as he fetched [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) with [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) and cast [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) of his own. On the surface the two [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) lists looked very similar as Jordan cracked his own Rainforest for [Lotus Cobra](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Cobra).


There was no third land for Chapin but he did muster a [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise). Jordan played a land that entered the battlefield tapped and took advantage of the blue mana he made with Cobra to play [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder). He then cast [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) copying Cobra.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm4%20Chapin.JPG)*Patrick Chapin*
Chapin found his land and played his own [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) -- copying Cobra -- and then played his Land into [Cunning Sparkmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cunning+Sparkmage) to take out Jordan's original Cobra. Problem was Jordan still had the copy and a fetch land allowed him to sweep the board with [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) and Chapin was ready to move onto the second game.


**Patrick Chapin - 0 Dan Jordan - 1** 


### Game Two


Patrick shuffled his entire deck into his sideboard and began pulling out the fifteen that were going on the bench. Jordan pulled out his notes and consulted his sideboarding guide that he had prepared from the event. There were more than a few alarmed looks as Jordan consulted his script but it was quickly explained by knowing friends that it was legal to do such things under the current floor rules.



![Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Solemn+Simulacrum)

Chapin shipped back his openers for a fresh six cards that let him get started with [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) which allowed for a turn two [Sea Gate Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sea+Gate+Oracle) to refresh his hand. Jordan came out of the gate more slowly with a tapped land and turn two [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain). [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) on Chapin's upkeep was his first real play to tap down the Birds. Chapin played [Sylvok Replica](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvok+Replica) and patiently passed the turn.


[Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) for [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) was Jordan's play and Chapin paid two life to [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph) his [Sea Gate Oracle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sea+Gate+Oracle). "Two cards?" asked Jordan. He tapped out to play [Urabrask the Hidden](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urabrask+the+Hidden). Chapin sent a pair of Sea Gates into the red zone. Jordan put his Exarch and Simulacrum in the path of one. [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) came down and did three damage to Ubarask. [Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt) finished off it and the Solemn that had just taken one from the Oracle


Jordan played [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) and Metamorph. He copied the Titan and took out a trio of elves and birds. Chapin sac'd his Replica and Jordan redirected the ability to his [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) with his last open blue mana. Jordan had three cards and Chapin had none -- he drew for his turn. [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder) found [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) for the Metamorph. Titan attacked and did 12 to Jordan who chose not to chump with his Exarch. He wanted to buy one more turn to rip a [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) off the top but it was not there and they were onto the rubber game.


**Patrick Chapin - 1 Dan Jordan - 1** 


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm4%20Jordan.JPG)*Dan Jordan*
### Game Three


Quick keeps on both sides and Jordan led off with [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) into [Ponder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ponder). it was a nearly Identical turn one from Chapin except he played [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain). Jordan summoned a pair of [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite)s while Chapin played [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) in between. Five points of total life change had occurred and it was entirely from fetch lands as Chapin broke the third in as many turns to power out [Vengevine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vengevine) and rumble in for 4.


Jordan passed the turn only to flash out [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) to tap the [Vengevine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vengevine) prior to attacking. Chapin played a fetch land and passed.



![Urabrask the Hidden](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Urabrask+the+Hidden)

"Cards in hand?" asked Jordan and the answer was five. He offered up [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod). When it resolved he sacrificed his Exarch for [Solemn Simulacrum](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemn+Simulacrum) and a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest). Chapin had [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) the [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) but Jordan dipped briefly to 10 -- and then up to 14 from [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) -- as he redirected it to a [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite). He fell back to 10 with no blocks on [Vengevine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vengevine). Chapin sacrificed land number four and number five to play [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan). He announced two points on Solemn and one on Jordan.


Jordan fell to 7 as he redirected the two to the Solemn to his [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) and went to 5 on his turn to Pod up Urabrask. He went to 4 from a fetch land to play a hasty [Inferno Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inferno+Titan) and did three to Chapin's Titan and another three when it attacked. The game looked like it was going Jordan's way -- especially with his [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) still at the ready but Chapin showed him a pair of [Act of Aggression](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Act+of+Aggression)s. He used the first on the [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) and then the second one on Urabrask to leave Jordan defenseless against his attack.


**Final result: Patrick Chapin - 2 Dan Jordan - 1** 




Friday, 4:30 p.m.: Draft One – Gettin' Sidetracked
--------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro* 


![Sorin's Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sorin%27s+Vengeance)

Right now, there are about two and a half pods worth of undefeated players. Going into the first draft, there are a good amount of people sitting at 4-0. Though it's easy to look at the first pod – at Brad Nelson and Luis Scott-Vargas – and call them the frontrunners, there's virtually no difference between Pod 1 and Pod 3. I hovered around the first table to see what Brad and his surrounding drafters had going on in the first *M12* draft of the weekend. But as you'll see, I got a little sidetracked.


Brad started strong with a first pick [Sorin's Vengeance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sorin%27s+Vengeance). He backed that pick up with a [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger) and other solid black. But Alex Smith to his right, also ventured into black from his first couple blue picks and cut some nice black picks from Nelson. Smith went black because to *his* right, Ali Aintrazi started snaking his blue after starting out in white. Brad didn't mind too much, there were still some good darkly colored pickings in [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton) and the like, and soon Nelson ventured into his own second color, green. After a couple [Arachnus Web](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arachnus+Web)s, and [Rampant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rampant+Growth)s Nelson's solid second color was stealing from the person on *his* right with an aggressive Green-White aggro deck.


So pretty much, all the players were drafting one color from their neighbor on the left, and one color from the neighbor to their right. It oddly worked out for all of them, and everyone wound up with pretty good – though not really remarkable – decks.



![Vengeful Pharaoh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Vengeful+Pharaoh)

Brad tried a red splash in pack three with a first-pick [Flameblast Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flameblast+Dragon) and a second-pick [Shock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shock), but ultimately decided against it in deck-building because of a late [Cudgel Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cudgel+Troll), [Sutured Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sutured+Ghoul) and [Overrun](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overrun) obviating the need for a third color.


Aintrazi wound up with a good U/W deck with seemingly infinite good five-drops: three [Chasm Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chasm+Drake), a [Djinn of Wishes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Djinn+of+Wishes) and a [Belltower Sphinx](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Belltower+Sphinx). Wesley Wise, a couple seats down (sitting next to Aintrazi), ended with a good black and red deck that curved out nicely. A couple [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night), Duskhunter (along with the appropriate one-drops), two [Gorehorn Minotaurs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gorehorn+Minotaurs), a [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin), a [Vengeful Pharaoh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vengeful+Pharaoh) and a [Flameblast Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flameblast+Dragon) of his own.


I started to survey Alex Smith's final list. It looked pretty good with a [Cemetery Reaper](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cemetery+Reaper), some [Ice Cage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ice+Cage)s, but then I got sidetracked. Sitting next to Smith during deckbuilding was Alex Bertoncini. He started poking me saying, "Hey, hey. Check it out." So, like a good journalist, I checked it out.


Bertoncini had drafted two [Rune-Scarred Demon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rune-Scarred+Demon)s and two [Diabolic Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diabolic+Tutor)s. He smiled sinisterly and said, "I mean I'm going to get tired from all the searching I'll be doing. It's a good thing I have *two [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball)s* to search for!" I scoured his cards. The pile he'd put together looked totally awesome, but fact-checking showed he didn't have two [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball)s, though. It was a [Fireball](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fireball) and a [Consume Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consume+Spirit). See? Good journalist.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Bertoncini%20Fan.JPG)*Alex Bertoncini*
"I wish I could play this though." Bertoncini frowned as he showed the [Sphinx of Uthuun](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx+of+Uthuun) in his sideboard. What a fun, ridiculous deck. It was totally cooler than these other decks I was looking at. But I'm a good journalist, right? I can stay on track. Stay on target; Stay on target. I was about to get back on the straight and narrow, then I ran into Nate Pease. And all hope was lost. Any semblance of these other standard, solid, if kinda-blah decks swiftly left my brain.


About Nate Pease's deck: So when you draft Black-Red Bloodthirst, what are you hoping for? Some solid one drops, right? How's three [Goblin Fireslinger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Fireslinger)s, two [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist)s and a [Tormented Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormented+Soul) ? Now those are all well and good, but they're actually pretty bad cards if your curve stumbles after that. You need at least a few great two-drops with hopefully one [Stormblood Berserker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stormblood+Berserker). How about three?! Yup, three highly sought-after uncommons in the two-drop slot (along with two [Blood Seeker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Seeker)s). And it doesn't stop after that. Pease continues to curve out perfectly with three [Bloodrage Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodrage+Vampire), a [Blood Ogre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Ogre), a Vampire Outcast and two [Gorehorn Minotaurs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gorehorn+Minotaurs). He even grabbed a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade) and some other sweet removal. Pease's last cut was the very solid [Bonebreaker Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonebreaker+Giant) for a measly [Goblin Piker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Piker).


"I needed to. The giant's too slow."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Pease%20Fan.JPG)*Nate Pease*
I swear guys, just because I ditched all the players at the first table to ogle Nate's and Alex's decks doesn't mean I have a short attention span. It just means I know a good story when I see one – like a good journalist. Right?




Round 5: Feature Match – Michael Jacob vs. David Ochoa
------------------------------------------------------


*by Brian David-Marshall* 

"Really," groaned Michael Jacob as he made his way to the feature match area. "No one wants to see this."


He was very unhappy with the deck he had drafted -- after going 3-1 in the Standard portion with RUG-Pod. For better or worse, when you are one of the most successful U.S. Nationals players in the room you are going to get featured regardless of the quality of your draft deck. Jacob has been on two different National teams. In 2008 he was the National champion and led a team with Sam Black and Paul Cheon to the World Team Championship in Memphis to close out the 2008 season.


"Am I playing this card?" laughed Jacob at one of his main deck inclusions. "Yes I am. Am I splashing for it? Also, yes."


His opponent David Ochoa came close to making the National team last season but ended up as the alternate instead. Ochoa is on the short list of top players who have yet to get a Pro Tour Top 8 on their resume. He came close last season with a 12th place finish in Amsterdam. His next Pro Point will be his 100th -- which a Top 16 finish would guarantee him.


### Game One


"I will draw!" said Jacob without any hesitation when he won the die roll. "Have you been manascrewed yet? Are you due?"


Ochoa maintained his trademark straight face and Jacob continued his patter about his draft: "I think more than one player at our table was forcing something."


Ochoa kept his opening hand and Jacob slumped: "There goes my way to win."


Neither player did anything on this first couple of turns until Ochoa plopped down a [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin) against two [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains).


"So that is how it is going to be," laughed Jacob, who played a third land and passed the turn. "You know what I have to say to that? Absolutely nothing. How did you know I would be weak to [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin)?"


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm5%20MJ.JPG)*Michael Jacob*
Ochoa played [Divination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divination) and dug into a [Distress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Distress).


"You figured me out," said Jacob sheepishly as he laid out a fistful of creatures and [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment). One of those creatures was [Goblin Bangchuckers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bangchuckers) -- the card he was embarrassed about earlier.


Jacob drew and played [Bonebreaker Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonebreaker+Giant) a turn later and Ochoa came back with [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade). Over the next few turns Jacob dumped [Griffin Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griffin+Sentinel), [Benalish Veteran](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Benalish+Veteran) and the Bangchuckers onto the board. Ochoa played [Æther Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Adept) and bounced the 'Chuckers.


"You think I am ever going to win a coin flip?" snorted Jacob.


Ochoa flew over for 5 with his [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade) and Jacob replayed the Goblin and took another five from the Shade. Jacob untapped and promptly used the Bangchuckers to try and kill the Assassin. Just to be safe, Ochoa used the Assassin in response. True to his word, Jacob lost the flip. Ochoa blocked the [Bonebreaker Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonebreaker+Giant) with his [Æther Adept](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Adept). When he played [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger) to get the Adept back, that was enough for Jacob to throw in the towel.


### Game Two


"Was that a first pick?" asked Jacob regarding Ochoa's [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin).


"No the guy who was in between us passed it to me," said Ochoa with just a hint of a grin.


Jacob, who had chosen to draw again, led off with [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist): "My secret tech to beat a [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin)."


Ochoa played [Alluring Siren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Alluring+Siren) and blocked the [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist) at first chance.


"There goes my out."


[Devouring Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devouring+Swarm) came down for Ochoa while Jacob played a second copy of the [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist): "Secret technology reveals itself again!"


Ochoa drew four extra cards over the next two turns with a pair of [Divination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divination)s sandwiching Jacob's [Griffin Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griffin+Sentinel). Ochoa also had [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton) to go along with the Swarm.


"Your deck is better than mine," frowned Jacob.


"Slightly," Ochoa deadpanned.


[Bonebreaker Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonebreaker+Giant) came down for Jacob while Ochoa flew over for two and added [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade). Things were looking good for the straight man in this comedy act. He had air superiority and [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton) to lock up the ground. Then things turned around for the former National Champion when he played [Spirit Mantle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit+Mantle) on the Bonebreaker. Jacob let the card linger in his hand for a second waiting to see if it was going to elicit any response from Ochoa.


"Yup," was all the California player could say. Jacob attacked with everything. Ochoae blocked the [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist) with Skeleton and then reassembled it to save the [Devouring Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devouring+Swarm). Jacob had [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) post combat for the Swarm. The life totals were 10 to 14 in Jacob's favor.


Ochoa still had the [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade) and took a four point bite out of Jacob's life total. [Divine Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Favor) graced the [Griffin Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griffin+Sentinel) and Jacob went up to 13 -- attacking Ochoa down to three. That was enough to send them to a third game.


### Game Three


While Jacob was off asking something of a judge Ochoa muttered some expletives about the card [Spirit Mantle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spirit+Mantle). He actually had very few cards in his deck to deal with it. There were a couple of counterspells and an [Unsummon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unsummon) but none of the [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade)s you might associate with the [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island)s and [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp)s he was playing.


"I will play," announced Ochoa, despite Jacob's clear enthusiasm for being on the draw. He had [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton) erected on turn two and Jacob was not happy about it. He played a second turn [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist).


Ochoa attacked for one with the Skeleton and Jacob was clearly surprised. "You have another one?!?"


[Devouring Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devouring+Swarm) was actually what was lurking on the other side of the attack step and Jacob nodded: "Oh the nutter butters." He played [Griffin Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griffin+Sentinel).


Ochoa attacked and then cast [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm5%20Ochoa.JPG)*David Ochoa*
An "Ugh" announced Jacob's next draw step. He got in for two and had no fourth turn play. Ochoa was hesitant about his next turn and wanted to attack with both fliers, then seemed like he was going to sit back -- not wanting to commit mana to protecting either of them -- and then finally attacking with both. The Shade was blocked by the Griffin and Ochoa pumped once -- then went in the tank before pumping a second time to try and kill it. Ochoa sac'd it to the Swarm in response to the [Chandra's Outrage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chandra%27s+Outrage) to counter the spell.


Ochoa went to 16 from Jacob's next attack. The former Nats Champ followed up with [Pacifism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pacifism) on the Swarm and [Crimson Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crimson+Mage).


Ochoa played [Divination](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divination) -- the card he was agonizing over on the previous turn -- and found a fifth land to also play [Distress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Distress). Lurking in Jacob's hand were [Volcanic Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Volcanic+Dragon) and the land to play it. He took the dragon.


Ochoa played [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger) to get back [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade) but had to wait a turn and took two from a freshly cast [Peregrine Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peregrine+Griffin) that was given haste by the Mage -- Ochoa went to 12.


Ochoa replayed the [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade) and braced for impact as Jacob added a hasty [Bonebreaker Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonebreaker+Giant). Jacob sent in the Giant, the 2/4 Griffin and the pesky [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist). Ochoa -- who only had two black mana untapped -- looked for productive blocks. He could not find any and eventually settled on having the Skeleton absorb the brunt of the Giant and took two in the air. He reassembled EOT


Ochoa attacked for one with [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade) which may not have been much but it was enough to turn on bloodthirst for [Vampire Outcasts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Outcasts) -- 4/4 with lifelink is much better than 2/2. He also played [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin).


Jacob could only peck away for one with his Sentinel. [Drifting Shade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drifting+Shade) struck back for six in the air. Sentinel kept plugging away but the momentum of the game had swung toward Ochoa. [Peregrine Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peregrine+Griffin) chumped the Shade. [Divine Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Favor) on the Sentinel made things interesting. [Vampire Outcasts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampire+Outcasts) joined the attack next turn and ultimately traded the blocking [Goblin Arsonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Arsonist) for his [Royal Assassin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Royal+Assassin) and four precious life points.


[Peregrine Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peregrine+Griffin) was [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak)ed and Jacob conceded.


**Final result: Michael Jacob - 1 David Ochoa - 2**




Vintage Deck Tech – [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) - [Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop) with Ryan Glackin
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

If you are a Vintage fan, you might remember the name Ryan Glackin. Last year, he sliced his way to a Top 8 at the 2010 Vintage Championships with his Noble Fish deck. This time around, he has changed gears, switching over to the artifact-laden Workshop deck, but this one has a twist.


"After a bit of testing, we switched over from Magus of the Moon to [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther). You can't ignore the interaction with [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph). Also, the blue decks, which Magus was in the deck to beat, have started to play more basic lands, so he just isn't as effective. Plus, with [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) so popular now, having the [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) to just kill him is very nice."


Here's a look at Glackin's deck:







#### Ryan Glackin


#####
