[Mana Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMana%5D+%5BCrypt%5D)


4
[Tangle Wire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BTangle%5D+%5BWire%5D)


3
[Jester's Cap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BJester%5D+%5BCap%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Ancient+Tomb)



















![Null Rod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Null+Rod)

This deck is basically an artifact-based control deck that uses a suite of disruptive artifacts to control an opponent's ability to play spells for enough time for a [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) or [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem) to finish them off. Cards like [Thorn of Amethyst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thorn+of+Amethyst), [Sphere of Resistance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphere+of+Resistance), [Trinisphere](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trinisphere), and the [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem) make spells more expensive while [Tangle Wire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tangle+Wire), [Strip Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strip+Mine), and [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) keep them from having the ever increasing amount of mana to pay. In addition to those, [Null Rod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Null+Rod), [Phyrexian Revoker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Revoker), and [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) just stop them from playing spells or abilities right out. While they're locked down, the 4 or more powered creatures start business. Now, as the game goes on, the lock gets less effective, consequently the size of the creatures really matters.


Usually, the games play out with the Workshop player setting up a good soft lock. A first-turn [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) off of an [Ancient Tomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Tomb) followed by a [Sphere of Resistance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphere+of+Resistance) or [Thorn of Amethyst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thorn+of+Amethyst) is usually a pretty good start. With that in place, a [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem) or [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) can come down to start to hack away at the opponent's life. After that, to keep them from being able to answer the threat du jour, a [Tangle Wire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tangle+Wire) can come down to keep their resources at bay while a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) keeps them strapped for mana. You also have a set of [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph)s for extra redundancy and versatility. It's the perfect string along.


It is easy to overlook this way to play the deck, though. When you see a deck that is capable of powering out a first-turn [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem) and following that with a [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) or two, most people start basking in their third-turn kill. However, this just isn't how Vintage usually works.



![Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Blightsteel+Colossus)

*Out with ![](https://web.archive.org/web/20161225105850im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/custom/wiz_autocard/wiz_manacost/manasymbols/colorless2.gif)![](https://web.archive.org/web/20161115194122im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/custom/wiz_autocard/wiz_manacost/manasymbols/blue.gif), courtesy of [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker).*


"Making a first-turn [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) is almost always a mistake. There are just too many decks out there that can just kill you if you don't find a way to disrupt them. If they resolve a [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault) and [Voltaic Key](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voltaic+Key) or land a [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker), which usually gets [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus) these days for a one-shot kill, you just lose. You can't give them a chance. You almost always want to set up a nice defense before you go for the kill. Admittedly, there are occasionally games you win by being incredibly aggressive, but they don't usuay go that way."


This deck is designed to deal with the large number of blue-based decks in the field. With cards like [Thorn of Amethyst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thorn+of+Amethyst) and [Sphere of Resistance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphere+of+Resistance) to keep them from playing too many inexpensive spells in one turn, as well as [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) for [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor), they seem to have a good amount of game against blue. In the mirror match, those cards that are so good in that matchup become incredibly useless. The sideboard takes care of that, though.


"In the mirror match, you just get rid of all of those Spheres and Thorns and bring in [Precursor Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Precursor+Golem)s and [Crucible of Worlds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crucible+of+Worlds) and go to beat them down. I had to win my last round that way."


Also hiding in the sideboard are [Jester's Cap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jester%27s+Cap)s, which are another good answer to the very threat-light Blue decks, as well as the necessary [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus), to deal with the graveyard decks.


This is a great example of a resource denial strategy that is not only completely viable, but quite powerful in Vintage right now. If you like setting your opponent in a vise and watching them squirm helplessly as you slowly squeeze, this is certainly the deck for you.




Round 6: Feature Match – Luis Scott-Vargas vs. Brad Nelson
----------------------------------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro* 

So Brad Nelson was pretty unhappy with his deck. He showed it to Brian Kibler after losing his last round to drop to 4-1. "This might be the worst M12 limited deck I've ever seen," was the first thing Kibler said. He followed that comment closely with, "If you're to win a match this draft, you a) have to get *extremely* lucky, while b) your opponent gets *extremely* unlucky."


"My deck is pretty terrible too." Luis Scott-Vargas returned.


The usually chipper Brad Nelson was slightly frowning and slumping in his chair. This draft had gotten the best of him. On a lighter note, to figure out who went first, Luis laid two cards face down and said, "Pick the better card for constructed. Don't worry, it's not close." Nelson flipped over a [Wurm's Tooth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wurm%27s+Tooth), while LSV showed a [Dragon's Claw](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon%27s+Claw).


"See? Not close. I'll play."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm6%20LSV.JPG)*Luis Scott-Vargas*

![Crimson Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Crimson+Mage)

### Game One


They both kept and LSV played a turn-two [Crimson Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crimson+Mage) off a [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) and a [Plains](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Plains). He then cast a [Divine Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Favor) on it the following turn and attacked into a [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton) that declined to block. When Scott-Vargas attacked again, Nelson's Skeleton happily joined the fray, because this time he was aided by a [Sacred Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sacred+Wolf). All three creatures went happily to the graveyard.


Scott-Vargas quickly refilled with an [Arbalest Elite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arbalest+Elite) and an [Auramancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Auramancer) returning the [Divine Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Favor). Nelson's refilling consisted of the Skeleton rising from the grave and a [Garruk's Companion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Garruk%27s+Companion). An un-aura'ed [Thran Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thran+Golem) and an [Auramancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Auramancer) attacked the following, making the totals 23-13 in Luis Scott-Vargas' favor. Brad's demeanor was getting lower, but it hadn't hit bottom yet. That came when he realized the [Divine Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Favor) on Luis' [Thran Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thran+Golem) also gave in Flying, in addition to First Strike, Trample. and +3/+5. Two turns later, Brad was at one. Three turns later, he was dead.


**Luis Scott-Vargas 1 – 0 Brad Nelson**


"I can see from the spells we cast that neither of us were exaggerating about our decks." Scott-Vargas said. Brad could only let out a slight chuckle.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/fm6%20Sad%20Brad.JPG)*Sad Brad*
### Game Two


Though Nelson went first, Scott-Vargas cast the inaugural spell in [Crown of Empires](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crown+of+Empires). A turn-four [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton) was Brad's sort-of response, to which Luis cast a [Rusted Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rusted+Sentinel).



![Thran Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Thran+Golem)

The Sentinel's power was clearly too imposing, so an [Arachnus Web](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arachnus+Web) answered it. LSV tried to add power with [Divine Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Divine+Favor), but before it could resolve, Nelson [Naturalize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Naturalize)d the Sentinel away.


Over a few turns LSV added a [Thran Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thran+Golem), [Blood Ogre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Ogre) (bloodthirsty, mind you) and a [Benalish Veteran](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Benalish+Veteran), who received a [Deathmark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathmark). Brad had another [Reassembling Skeleton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reassembling+Skeleton) and a [Rusted Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rusted+Sentinel) of his own. There was an old fashioned stalemate round these parts.


That is, until Scott-Vargas cast a [Flameblast Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flameblast+Dragon).


Brad scoffed, drew his next card, and packed it in. I guess to Kibler's comment, neither a) nor b) happened for Brad. I didn't see him getting any happier as he walked away from the table.


**Luis Scott-Vargas 2 – 0 Brad Nelson**


Luis Scott-Vargas is now 5-1; Brad Nelson is 4-2.




Vintage Deck Tech – [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)/[Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush) Control with Stephen Menendian
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/dt%20menendian.JPG)*Stephen Menendian*
Stephen Menendian has long been a leading voice in the Vintage field. He has been a Vintage Champion, in 2007, as well as netting himself a spot in the 2007 **Magic** Invitational, the very last one. He is constantly on the front edge of design for Vintage, as a frequent contributor to the ever-growing community of Vintage writers.


It is a rare day when you can see Menendian sitting down to a Vintage match without [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) in his deck. One of the most powerful card-drawing engines ever made, the efficiently brutal Confidant is an integral part of Menendian's plan. Here's a look at what he brought to battle:

##### Mythic (20)



4

2
[Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSensei%5D+%5BDivining%5D+%5BTop%5D)


1
[Fastbond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BFastbond%5D)


1
[Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BYawgmoth%5D+%5BWill%5D)


1
[Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BTinker%5D)


1
[Mystical Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMystical%5D+%5BTutor%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Scalding+Tarn)


















When I first looked through his decklist, there were a few things that threw me off the trail of what this deck wanted to do. First, was the presence of [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique), [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator), and [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Those cards are all incredibly powerful, especially in Vintage. However, they all attack for real damage. At first, I thought that this deck might just be a control deck that beat opponents down with these dorks over a few turns until they were dead. That didn't seem too cool to me. I saw the [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker) and the [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus), but I figured they were just a way to grab an easy win out of nowhere. After watching Menendian play a couple of rounds, I realized that they weren't just tossed in the deck. They were the deck.


"Basically, this deck just wants to [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker) out a Colossus every game. That's its goal. Every other card in the deck is just there to make sure that it does that."


With that, I took another glance at the list. Well, yeah, there are Confidants and Cliques and Predators, but they really are just geared to make sure that he can grab a [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker) and get the Colossus into play as soon as possible. The Confidants draw him an absurd number of cards, helping him find it. The Predators keep the board free from anything that might stop him. The Cliques work double duty, acting as a form of end-step permission as well as targeting himself if the Colossus is stuck in his hand. Everything else in the deck, all the spells, are simply ways to draw, tutor, or protect his two-card combo.



![Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gush)
![Fastbond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Fastbond)

One of the things he was most excited about was the unrestriction of [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush).


"That is one of the biggest things to happen to Vintage this past year. Combined with [Fastbond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fastbond), it's an incredible combo. You get access to not only the cards that you get to draw, but replaying the lands gives you extra mana as well. Add in [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will), and you get to replay them all over again, getting even more cards and mana. It's pretty insane. With [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush), Confidant, and all of these Tutors, I have a lot of redundancy in getting the cards I need."


The interesting thing is how his plan is able to change drastically against different decks while not really changing at all.


"Against the Workshop decks, all I want to do, at any cost, is get a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) to stay in play. Against Dredge, all I want is a [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void)."


Against these decks, his target cards change, but the engine of the deck, the part of the deck that does the bulk of the work, doesn't change at all. Instead of doing anything to protect the [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker), he substitutes in a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) or the [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void). The deck's target changes, but its focus never does.


We talked a little about the state of Vintage right now, as it seemed to be going through a bit of a renaissance.



![Flusterstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Flusterstorm)

"Yeah, Vintage is in a really good place right now. There have been a number of new cards that have been released that have had an immediate impact on the format. You've got [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus), [Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep), [Steel Sabotage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steel+Sabotage) and [Leonin Relic-Warder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leonin+Relic-Warder) are seeing some play, [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) and [Phyrexian Revoker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Revoker) are really hot right now. [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph) is just amazing in the Workshop decks. I don't know if you can beat a first-turn [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem) that gets copied on the next turn. I'm even starting to see some [Flusterstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flusterstorm) from Commander floating around. This has been a very exciting year for Vintage.


About the only thing that might make it more interesting were if [Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction) were to be unrestricted. It's a good card, but not great anymore. It's just worse than [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor). But it would provide another interesting option for the blue decks out there. You've got all kinds of different blue decks out there, and a card like that would have a different effect on all of them. The best part is that it might actually make a slow blue deck more viable. There was a guy I saw yesterday playing a blue deck featuring [Intuition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Intuition) and [Accumulated Knowledge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Accumulated+Knowledge) and doing pretty well. [Fact or Fiction](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fact+or+Fiction) would be great for those decks, and simply another reasonable option for the faster decks in the field."



![Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mental+Misstep)

When I asked him how that might affect the non-blue decks in the format, he assured me that it wouldn't really matter.


"The thing is, the card is just slow right now. It is a lot of mana for an effect that isn't as good as it once was. Those decks aren't going to be hurt by it at all. It's not like it makes the blue decks in the format any better, it just has the potential to make them different. It may even open up a new deck type."


With that said, we talked a little more about his deck. With a deck that has so much card selection in it, despite the clear goal in mind, it seemed pretty difficult to play.


"Yeah, the decision tree is pretty complex on every turn. There are just so many decisions to make, and making the wrong one can really hurt you. This doesn't operate like the combo decks in the field, where they build up to a really big turn. This deck gains incremental advantages over a few turns until it's safe to slam the Colossus in there. Mistakes make those advantage smaller, and they can really affect the game."


The moral is to not let Vintage fool you. As simple as some of the plans seem for these decks, implementation of them is actually quite difficult. With access to whatever you want whenever you want, making the right decision is like finding a needle in a haystack. There may be multiple right answers, but only one that is most right. In a deck like this, finding the most right play every time takes lots and lots of practice. You'd better get started.




Round 7: Feature Match – Phillip Lorren vs. Haibing Hu
------------------------------------------------------


*by Steve Sadin* 

Phillip Lorren and Haibing Hu entered the final round of Day One with 6-0 records – the winner of this match would end the day as one of only two or three players in the tournament with a perfect 7-0 record – putting himself an arm's reach away from advancing to the Top 8. The loser would still be in excellent shape to make a run at the National Team with a 6-1 record.


Phillip Lorren has been playing limited for about 7 years, but he only started actively trying to qualify for the Pro Tour this past year. Lorren played in a bunch of *[Scar](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scar)s of Mirrodin* Sealed deck/Booster Draft PTQs for Pro Tour Paris, but he ultimately fell short of qualifying for the French PT. Unwilling to wait until the next limited qualifier season, Lorren gave himself a constructed crash course before competing at Grand Prix Atlanta, and Grand Prix Dallas. Lorren didn't make Day Two at either of those events, but he designed a Grixis Tezzeret deck which a friend of his took to a Top 32 finish at Grand Prix Dallas.


Lorren seems to be a quick learner though, as he has already gotten off to a 6-0 start this weekend.


Haibing Hu has been playing since Urza's Saga, but he "took some time off here and there." Hu played in his first Pro Tour nearly a decade ago (Pro Tour Nice in 2002), then played in another 4 or 5 Pro Tours with a few money finishes along the way. Hu has found some more time to play in tournaments recently, and came a fraction of a tiebreaker point away from earning money, and a Pro Point at Grand Prix Kansas City where he finished in 65th place.


Hu didn't practice a ton of Standard for this event, and explained that he was feeling his lack of preparation in Round 1 where he made a bunch of misplays. He was able to eek out a victory there, and then "tightened up," rattling off another five victories before entering this match.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Round%207%20-%20Hu.JPG)*Haibing Hu*
### Game One


Lorren won the roll and chose to play first, but he was unhappy with his opening hand and went down to six cards.


Even though Lorren mulliganed down to six cards, he had no shortage of removal spells.


Hu's [Goblin Fireslinger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Fireslinger) fell at the hands of [Wring Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wring+Flesh). [Crimson Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crimson+Mage) was able to swing in, once, but it ultimately died to Lorren's [Consume Spirit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consume+Spirit). A [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) countered Hu's [Duskhunter Bat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskhunter+Bat). And Hu's [Blood Ogre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Ogre) got killed by a [Doom Blade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doom+Blade).


Hu's [Tormented Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormented+Soul) was able to stick around, and he was also able to add an [Adaptive Automaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Adaptive+Automaton) (naming Ogre) to his board.


After using four removal spells, Lorren finally added a creature of his own to the board – a [Tormented Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormented+Soul) which he enchanted with [Dark Favor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Favor).


Hu's [Shock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shock) took out the 4/2 [Tormented Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormented+Soul), but Lorren was able to bring it back with a [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger). An [Act of Treason](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Act+of+Treason) on [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger) then knocked Lorren down to 9.


Lorren spent his turn casting a [Tormented Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormented+Soul) and a [Blood Seeker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Seeker), prompting Hu to keep the pressure on by Incinerating Lorren's [Gravedigger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gravedigger) and attacking in for three leaving Lorren on a meager 6 life.


Lorren never managed to draw an answer for his opponent's unblockable 1/1 – and a [Shock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shock) and a few more pecks from his [Tormented Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tormented+Soul) were enough to allow Hu to take game one.


**Haibing Hu 1 – Phillip Lorren 0**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Round%207%20-%20Loren.JPG)*Round 7 - Loren.JPG*
### Game Two


Lorren again chose to play first, and this time he had to mulligan down to five cards. Lorren did manage to make the first play of the game, a [Warpath Ghoul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warpath+Ghoul), but it died to Hu's [Shock](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shock) seconds after hitting the battlefield.


Hu cast an [Adaptive Automaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Adaptive+Automaton) naming "elemental" (representing [Lightning Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Elemental)), then followed it up with a second [Adaptive Automaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Adaptive+Automaton) also naming "elemental", allowing him to attack in for three with his first [Adaptive Automaton](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Adaptive+Automaton).


Lorren cast a [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night), then followed it up with a [Bloodrage Vampire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodrage+Vampire) – but Hu had an [Incinerate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Incinerate) to take out his opponent's 3/1.


Lorren attacked in with his [Child of Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Child+of+Night), but had no followup play. Hu had the [Lightning Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Elemental) which he had been representing for a few turns, but Lorren (who had started the game by mulliganing to five) had no answer, allowing Hu to end Day One with a perfect 7-0 record.


Final Result:


**Haibing Hu 2 – Phillip Lorren 0**




Player Profile – Brendan Hurst
------------------------------


*by Marc Calderaro* 


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Hurst%20-%20not%20smiling.JPG)

**Age:** 24  
**Occupation:** Johns Hopkins Research Assistant  
**Largest Magic Accomplishment:** Qualifying for this event


Brendan looks tired. Real tired. And for good reason – he's had the biggest day of his Magic career so far. He went 4-0 in Standard with the underrepresented [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle), and he just 3-1'ed his second ever *M12* draft in a long, hard-fought battle against a deck with more than one [Overrun](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overrun). The match ended in that way we know all too well – just the two of them at seemingly endless, empty table, being watched closely by a judge.


"It's been a long day," he told me.


However, for Brendan, it's been a relatively short career. He starting played **Magic** with *9th Edition* in college, but didn't start thinking about competitive **Magic** until two years ago, after graduation.


Hailing from Downingtown, PA, about an hour outside Philadelphia, Brendan decided to try his hand at the higher echelon of **Magic** for an interesting reason. ![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Hurst%20-%20smiling.JPG) "Most things I like to do, luckily, come fairly easy to me, but Magic has been very hard. I wanted to see if I could do well at something I had to work for." Though his highest accomplishments before this point were a couple PTQ Top 8s, it would seem that such work is beginning to pay off.


As far as his long-term **Magic** ambitions, they seem unclear. Brendan just wants to see how far the rabbit hole goes. Quite frankly, I think that's how a lot of us ended up where we are in **Magic** to this day. Because let me tell you something, the hole is deep. So don't be surprised if Brendan's in it for the long haul, and just doesn't know it yet.


At X-1, Hurst is positioned well for a spot on the National team this weekend. And if he can repeat today's performance again, you just might be seeing him in a bigger spotlight than this Player Profile. But for now, just think about the best **Magic** day you've ever had, think about how Brendan must feel right now and enjoy how truly tired he looks in these pictures. Especially the one where he tries to give me a smile.






Top 8 Vintage – Player Profiles
-------------------------------


*by Nate Price*


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Menendian.JPG)

**Name:** Stephen Menendian  
**Age:** 31  
**Hometown:** Columbus, Ohio  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** 17 years  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** 7 times, with one win  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** The Soldier  
**What deck did you play, and why?**[Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)/[Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush) control, because [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush) are two of the top draw engines in Vintage. Paul Mastriano is playing my deck too  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?**<[Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther)  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?**[Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush)  
**If you could take home another recommissioned piece of art, like the [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) being given away here today, what would you like to see done?**[Sol Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sol+Ring)





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Brown.JPG)

**Name:** Joseph Charles Brown  
**Age:** 30  
**Hometown:** Wilkes-Barre, Pennsylvania  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** Actively since 2010, casually since Revised  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** This is my first Vintage Championships  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** Alternate Universe in Blue Bell, Pennsylvania, Full of Win Games in Clarks Summit Pennsylvania, Topdeck Games in Westmont, New Jersey  
**What deck did you play, and why?** Bishop's Painter. The Vintage metagame has become very blue heavy, and this version prey on blue decks  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?** Mike Noble creating [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther).dec  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?**[Timetwister](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Timetwister)  
**If you could take home another recommissioned piece of art, like the [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) being given away here today, what would you like to see done?**[Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault)





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Mastriano.JPG)

**Name:** Paul Mastriano  
**Age:** 29  
**Hometown:** Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** 1996 – when they called it "Type One"  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** Played four times, made the top 8 three times, won in 2008.  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** Blue Bell, Pennsylvania and New York  
**What deck did you play, and why?** Meandeck [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush)-[Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) – I play a tournament almost every weekend and my teammates and I felt the two best decks were [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush) and Suicide Jace Vault. Our deck is a combination of the two.  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?** The [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) Oath deck  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?**[Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk)  
**If you could take home another recommissioned piece of art, like the [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) being given away here today, what would you like to see done?** Awesome Vintage-only staples: [Mana Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Drain), [Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop), [Mana Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Crypt), [Sol Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sol+Ring), [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad), [Tolarian Academy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tolarian+Academy), [Library of Alexandria](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Library+of+Alexandria), [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault)





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Shay.JPG)

**Name:** Rich Shay  
**Age:** 30  
**Hometown:** Norwood, Massachusetts (currently in Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania)  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** Since Unlimited  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** Four times, second place  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** The university center at Carnegie Mellon University  
**What deck did you play, and why?**[Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush). It is explosive and powerful, and also able to drag opponents into long games. It combines good qualities of control decks and combo decks  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?**[Mental Misstep](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mental+Misstep) and cutting [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault)  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?**[Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush), since [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and Mindslave see play in other formats  
**If you could take home another recommissioned piece of art, like the [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) being given away here today, what would you like to see done?**[Library of Alexandria](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Library+of+Alexandria)! Or… [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad)!!! Also, [Library of Alexandria](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Library+of+Alexandria) (especially).





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Bogaard.JPG)

**Name:** Joseph Bogaard  
**Age:** 23  
**Hometown:** Chicago, Illinois  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** 7-8 years  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** I have played twice – this is my best finish  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** I don't have anywhere  
**What deck did you play, and why?** BUG Fish, because I felt comfortable with it after the preliminaries on Thursday, and it has strong pre-board games vs blue and workshop decks.  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?**[Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) is still good even in a format with [Ancestral Recall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Recall) and [Black Lotus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Lotus)  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?** I love casting [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will), even though I am not playing it today  
**If you could take home another recommissioned piece of art, like the [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) being given away here today, what would you like to see done?**[Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad), [Library of Alexandria](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Library+of+Alexandria), [Mana Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Drain), [Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop), [Tolarian Academy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tolarian+Academy), [Sol Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sol+Ring), [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will)





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Glackin.JPG)

**Name:** Ryan Glackin  
**Age:** 31  
**Hometown:** Philadelphia, Pennsylvania  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** Semi-competitively, about 5 years. Casually, forever.  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** Four times. I made top 8 last year  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** Alternate Universes, Blue Bell. Brothers Grimm, Selden New York, soon to be Top Deck Games, Westmont New Jersey.  
**What deck did you play, and why?** Cat Stax Fever, because I've been running pretty well with it lately. Also because blue decks give me headaches  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?**[Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther) and [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph). Decks built by Mike Noble consisting mostly of 4-ofs.  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?**[Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther)! Meow!  
**If you could take home another recommissioned piece of art, like the [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) being given away here today, what would you like to see done?**[Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop)





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Hornung.JPG)

**Name:** Mark Hornung Jr.  
**Age:** 23  
**Hometown:** Philadelphia, Pennsylvania  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** Two years  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** Twice, with my best finish so far being 17th.  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** With Nick Coss or Nick Detwiler  
**What deck did you play, and why?** It's Always Sunny in Philadelphia [[Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan) Dredge] because Matt Elias said I am a pro deck flipper.  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?** Mike Noble creating Mike Noble Fish and Cat Stax Fever  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?**[Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad) (obv!)





![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/Vin%20T8%20Coss.JPG)

**Name:** Nicholas Coss  
**Age:** 26  
**Hometown:** Moorestown, New Jersey  
**How long have you been playing Vintage?** Eight years.  
**How many times have you played in the Vintage Championship, and what was your best finish?** Three times, 11th last year, top 8 this year  
**Where do you play Vintage locally?** I run the Philadelphia area Vintage tournaments, so I don't get to play as often as I like. NYSE tournaments are great when I get the chance to play.  
**What deck did you play, and why?** "Minus Six" AKA [Worldgorger Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Worldgorger+Dragon) combo. It is very resilient for a combo deck, and it is very fast.  
**What is the coolest recent innovation or new card to hit Vintage?** Mike Noble seeing the power of [Slash Panther](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slash+Panther), and creating "Cat Stax Fever"  
**What is your favorite Vintage-only card?**[Yawgmoth's Bargain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Bargain)  
**If you could take home another recommissioned piece of art, like the [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) being given away here today, what would you like to see done?**[Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad), [Mishra's Workshop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Workshop) or [Mana Drain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Drain)

Vintage Quarterfinals Roundup
-----------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

### Quarterfinal 1 – Stephen Menendian vs. Joseph Bogaard


Things didn't start too auspiciously for Menendian, as Bogaard managed a first-turn [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) to strip the [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker) that was in Menendian's hand. With his method of getting his [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus) in the graveyard, his entire plan came down to resolving a [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will). Getting the resources in play to put all of that together became a difficult proposition, as Bogaard got [Life from the Loam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Life+from+the+Loam) and [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) going to keep Menendian off of his lands. Menendian did have a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) in play to ensure a steady stream of lands to keep afloat. Bogaard resolved a [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) at one point, and it looked lost, until Menendian managed to draw a [Fastbond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fastbond), allowing him to combine with multiple copies of [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush) to squeeze enough mana out of his two lands to cast [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will), [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker), and [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) all in one turn. The new [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus) ate Jace one turn before infecting Bogaard to deck in an incredible turn of fate.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vqfBrownMenendian.jpg)*Joseph Brown and Stephen Menendian*
The second game was considerably less intense. Bogaard was stuck on one land after a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), meaning he had a pair of useless cards on top of his deck. Fortunately for him, Menendian made a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), giving him a target for his sideboarded [Darkblast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Darkblast), allowing him to dredge those two cards away. Menendian made a second [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) over the next two turns, while Bogaard tried desperately to find another land. He eventually found a [Strip Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strip+Mine), but the game was out of reach. In an unusual fashion, Menendian relied on actual damage to kill his opponent.


**Stephen Menendian 2 – Joseph Bogaard 0**


### Quarterfinals 2 – Ryan Glackin vs. Joseph Brown


Glackin's Cat Stax deck got a really fast grip on the first game, using a [Mana Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Crypt+)  and a [Black Lotus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Lotus) to literally power out a [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) for one and a [Sphere of Resistance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphere+of+Resistance). He managed to keep Brown locked down with a [Strip Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strip+Mine) as his two Mishra's Factories, one of which started life as a [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph), ground him to dust.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vqfBogaardGlackin.jpg)*Joseph Bogaard and Ryan Glackin*
The second game was about as anticlimactic as the first. Glackin locked down Brown's artifact mana early with a [Null Rod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Null+Rod), keeping him very restricted on mana. He would have found himself able to deal with it, but he had used his one artifact-removal spell, an [Ingot Chewer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ingot+Chewer), on the previous turn to kill a [Thorn of Amethyst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thorn+of+Amethyst). Locked down under that [Null Rod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Null+Rod), Brown's problems were exacerbated thanks to a [Strip Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strip+Mine) and a [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) from Glackin. With Brown locked down, a [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem) took his sweet time to bash Brown down.


**Ryan Glackin 2 – Joseph Brown 0**


### Quarterfinals 3 – Paul Mastriano vs. Rich Shay


In this quarterfinals match, Mastriano was able to assemble a near-perfect opening set of turns, using a [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk), [Vampiric Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampiric+Tutor), and a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) to set up a third-turn [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will) with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) backup. Shay, who had gone undefeated in the swiss, had the [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to keep Mastriano honest, but once the Will resolved, the game was more or less over. Mastriano got to recast [Vampiric Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampiric+Tutor) and [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) to get a [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker)ed [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus) into play. Shay had no answer, and the first game went to Mastriano


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vqfMastrianoShay.jpg)*Paul Mastriano and Rich Shay*
The next game was a textbook example of explosive Vintage at its finest. Shay mulliganned to six cards, but those six cards contained a [Mox Sapphire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Sapphire) and a [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker), resulting in a second-turn [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus). Seemed pretty good. Pretty good until Mastriano drew [Black Lotus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Lotus) for his turn. Then, after a significant amount of thought and talking through his decision tree, he played Lotus, [Sol Ring](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sol+Ring), [Voltaic Key](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voltaic+Key), and then [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk). On his second turn, he dropped a [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault) into play, to which Shay could do nothing but concede. You can threaten a third-turn kill and find yourself conceding five minutes later. Welcome to Vintage!


**Paul Mastriano 2 – Rich Shay 0**


### Quarterfinals 4 – Mark Hornung vs. Nick Coss


This was possibly the most interesting match to me initially, since both players were playing decks that have been so powerful at one point, that they define sideboards to this day. Because they demand so much hate, they are often deemed unplayable in the current metagame. I am of course talking about Dredge and [Worldgorger Dragon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Worldgorger+Dragon).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vqfHornungCoss.jpg)*Mark Hornung and Nick Coss*
The first game went pretty standardly for both players. They each mulliganned until they found their [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad), using them to dredge their libraries until their graveyards towered over them. Unfortunately, Coss wasn't able to assemble his combo, or another answer, faster than the [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below) could churn out all of the Zombies ever. Needless to say, with that many Zombies, not even Woody Harrelson could survive.


The second game went exactly the opposite way, but for a very unorthodox reason. Nick Coss went to the board for an incredibly surprise way to win. Needless to say, Hornung was probably a little surprised when he only got one activation of his [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad) before Coss managed to assemble [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault) and [Voltaic Key](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voltaic+Key). That's right, from the board, he stuck the combo into his deck, knowing full well that his graveyard was not going to be how he won this match. When he played the [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault), Hornung had a chance to stop it from happening. He had a single copy of [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) in his graveyard, and could flash it back to try and stop the combo. He had to choose between [Vampiric Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampiric+Tutor), which Coss could cast on upkeep to fetch the Key, or [Voltaic Key](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voltaic+Key) itself. He said that something was telling him [Vampiric Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampiric+Tutor), so he chose the powerful instant. Something lied to him. When Coss revealed his hand, showing the Key that was coming down on his turn, Hornung conceded.


"Man, I thought I had picked right, too."


The final game was right back to the first. Hornung just absolutely went off. He showed off the newest addition to the deck, getting a massive dredge off early. With his graveyard getting full, he cast [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return) to bring back [Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan), getting back a dredged Bazaar, which he used to refill his graveyard, which gave him more [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return) fodder, so he could keep recurring [Sun Titan](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sun+Titan) to get more Bazaars and so on. Eventually, he had so many Zombies that he had to borrow more tokens. Coss made him go through the motions, just to rib a friend, and packed it in when the Zombies hit home.


**Mark Hornung 2 – Nick Coss 1**




Vintage Championship Semifinals Roundup
---------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

### Semifinal 1 – Mark Hornung vs. Ryan Glakin


These guys are pretty good friends, so the banter between them was nice and snarky.


"Bad luck, and I hope you mulligan into oblivion," Glackin said to Hornung with a smile.


Hornung did what he was supposed to do in the first game, mulliganning to five cards, including one that involved a [Serum Powder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serum+Powder), all in an attempt to find a [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad). Once he found it, he started to get his dredge cards into his bin. Unfortunately, he only got one activation before it was removed with [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland). He had a second copy of Bazaar, allowing him to dredge a load of cards into his graveyard, but Glackin had a [Strip Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strip+Mine) for the second one. After that, Glackin put together a [Lodestone Golem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lodestone+Golem), a [Phyrexian Metamorph](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Metamorph) copying the Golem, and a [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) for one just to be safe. Those Golems wasted very little time in wasting Hornung.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20sf%20hornung.jpg)*Mark Hornung gets his Dredge on.*
The second game went considerably differently. Hornung again mulliganed, this time to six cards, and again found two copies of [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad). This time, however, Glackin had nothing more than a [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) on one as defense. With the way clear, Hornung set about using his two Bazaars, a trio of [Golgari Grave-Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Grave-Troll)s, and a pair of [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return)s to put eight Zombies into play alongside an 8/8 Grave-Troll on the second turn. Glakin was not equipped to deal with that and the match went to the final game.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20sf%20zombies.jpg)*BRAAAINS!*
For the final game, Glackin went first and exploded with a [City of Traitors](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=City+of+Traitors) and a [Mana Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Crypt), enabling a [Chalice of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chalice+of+the+Void) for one and a [Thorn of Amethyst](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thorn+of+Amethyst) before Hornung played a permanent. Hornung simply (and I say that sarcastically) played a [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad). Glackin made a Percursor Golem to follow that up, putting nine power worth of creatures onto the table on the second turn. Hornung started to dredge, putting a dozen cards into his graveyard. Glackin animated his [Mishra's Factory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mishra%27s+Factory) and attacked for eleven. Hornung only had one turn, but, as dredge does, only needed one turn. He dredged a literal ton, playing an [Undiscovered Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Undiscovered+Paradise) so that he could play his [Dread Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dread+Return) through the Thorn, netting himself twelve very fast, very angry Zombies that crushed over Glackin and dropped him out of the Top 8.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20sf%20glackin.jpg)*Even with all those Golems, Ryan Glackin knows he's done.*
**Mark Hornung 2 – Ryan Glackin 1**


### Semifinals 2 – Stephen Menendian vs. Paul Mastriano


In a rematch from the swiss rounds, Stephen Menendian squared off against a virtually identical deck being piloted by Paul Mastriano. Menendian had won their initial showdown, and Mastriano was out for some friendly vengeance. Their first game started with two [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)s apiece, setting the stage for a fairly quick first game. I realized during this match that there is nothing quite as funny as watching people decide whether or not they should block an opponent's Confidant with their own. At one point during the game, there was a crucial near miss where Menendian drew a [Merchant Scroll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merchant+Scroll) and a [Preordain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Preordain) with his Confidants, leaving him to draw the [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus) that would have killed him during his draw step. That was a pretty lucky order for that to happen.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20sf%20mastriano.jpg)*Paul Mastriano knows it's a Bob eat Bob world.*
Their Confidants kept hitting themselves and then each other, whittling away the life totals. Eventually, Menendian was forced to a difficult decision about whether or not to use a freshly cast [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) to block a Confidant, saving him two life, or to let them through, drop his opponent to two on the swing back, and hope his two Confidants kill him. He chose the latter decision, and the suspense of the moment was proven to be quite anticlimactic. He untapped and flipped over [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) and [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant), killing him even if he had blocked.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20sf%20menendian.jpg)*To block, or not to block. That, is Menendian's question.*
For the second game, neither player had an early [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant). Mastriano went down to zero lands to [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush), which prompted Menendian to [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush) himself down to a [Mox Jet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Jet) before using [Red Elemental Blast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Red+Elemental+Blast) to stop Mastriano's copy. Both players managed a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) on the next turn, and things progressed rather slowly for a couple of turns until Mastriano managed to stick a [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault). Menendian stuck a [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) end of turn, revealing the two-headed monster of [Voltaic Key](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voltaic+Key) and [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker) in Mastriano's grip. He ended up choosing to put the Key at the bottom of the deck.


When Menendian played [Fastbond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fastbond), it looked like he might be able to find a way out of his little pickle. A fight ensued over Menendian's [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush), clearing the way for him to cast [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will). Unfortunately, his life total was incredibly low, severely restricting the amount of [Gush](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gush)ing he could do. Ultimately, Menendian had to use a [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) simply to untap. Mastriano spent the next few turns simply using powerful cards like [Black Lotus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Lotus) and [Ancestral Recall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Recall) to draw the counters out of Menendian's hand. Each turn that he did, though, Menendian's [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) slammed over for another three. Eventually, it was the last three.


Menendian got the final game rolling with an early [Fastbond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fastbond). Combined with a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and a [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top), he had a dominating early board position, but he ended the turn with only a single card in his hand. At the end of his turn, Mastriano used a [Vampiric Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampiric+Tutor) to fetch up a [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker), which he immediately used to trade his [Mox Emerald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Emerald) in for a [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus). Menendian did put on a little show in response, using his Top to hunt for an answer, but didn't find anything to stop it. He now had only his turn to deal with the Colossus or Mastriano. When he fetched a [Hurkyl's Recall](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hurkyl%27s+Recall) with his [Demonic Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Demonic+Tutor) on the following turn, Mastriano had the [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) to just put the match to an end.


**Stephen Menendian 1 – Paul Mastriano 2**




Vintage Finals – Paul Mastriano vs. Mark Hornung
------------------------------------------------


*by Nate Price* 

### Game One


Hornung started the first game off with a [Serum Powder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serum+Powder), followed by a mulligan to six…then five, all in search of a [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad). He found it, and they were off. Both players made a show of the early turns of the game. Hornung used his Bazaar to start his dredge engine, building up a massive graveyard on the second turn. Mastriano played a Mox and a [Black Lotus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Black+Lotus) in addition to his land to put him up to five mana before letting Hornung do his worst.


Well, his worst seemed to be pretty good. Dredging a significant portion of his library into his graveyard on his turn, he played a land to bring back a couple of [Bloodghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodghast)s, which he used to cast a pair of Cabal Therapies, stripping the [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) from Mastriano's hand. Mastriano was stuck facing a formidable army of [Bridge from Below](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bridge+from+Below) Zombies before untapping for his second turn. When he did, he simply made a [Trygon Predator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trygon+Predator) and passed the turn with a [Mox Sapphire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mox+Sapphire) up. Undeterred, Hornung did what his deck does, milling his deck, getting back [Narcomoeba](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Narcomoeba)s (which he remembered this time), sacrificing them for various things, and vomiting Zombies of various shapes and sizes onto the table. Combined with his Flame-kin Zealot, the hasty and large army of Zombies smashed in for way more than lethal. Mastriano chump blocked one of the Zombies with his Trygon, while the rest of the Zombies dropped him to approximately negative brazillion.


**Paul Mastriano 0 – Mark Hornung 1**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20f%20hornung.JPG)### Game Two


Stephen Menendian, who was playing 73 of the same cards as Mastriano, admitted after the first game that Mastriano only had about a 5% chance of winning the first game. Things get significantly better when he gets to put the large amount of sideboard hate that has limited the sideboard space of every deck in Vintage since the word Dredge was first printed on a card. One of those cards is [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void), which Mastriano managed to find after a mulligan to six. Putting the hate-filled enchantment into play on his side, Mastriano played a [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle) as well, naming [Bazaar of Baghdad](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bazaar+of+Baghdad). With those two cards in play, Hornung was virtually dead. When a second Leyline hit play, the game was absolutely sealed. Hornung wasn't able to find the absurd number of [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim)s he needed to be able to use his cards before Mastriano was able to drop [Voltaic Key](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voltaic+Key) and [Time Vault](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Vault), assembling the Time Machine, and take as many turns as necessary to win the game.


**Paul Mastriano 1 – Mark Hornung 1**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20f%20mastriano.JPG)Well, that was certainly a different game than the first. This time around, rather than being the whipping boy as Dredge ran rampant on him, Mastriano was able to completely exert his will on Hornung, completely locking him out of the game, much as Hornung had done to him.


The second game started out in similar fashion, much to the dismay of Hornung. Mastriano started with a [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void) before drawing into a [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle). The trio of Moxen in his hand allowed Mastriano to get a massive advantage, as well as locking Hornung's deck strategy up. Hornung used his Bazaar one time before it got locked off, trading his three worst cards for an opportunity to draw into a [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim)…or two. He did manage to find one, which immediately ate the [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void). Trying to end things before Hornung could get back into the game, Mastriano used a [Vampiric Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vampiric+Tutor) to snag a [Tinker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tinker), allowing him to get a [Blightsteel Colossus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blightsteel+Colossus). For his draw step, Hornung went yard, ripping a [Chain of Vapor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chain+of+Vapor) to send the Colossus packing. In addition, he had another [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) to free his Bazaar from the [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle)! Welcome to Vintage, where you can be guaranteed victory one moment and have your back against the wall in the next.


But, like had been happening all game, Mastriano had the perfect card to keep things under control. He used a [Yawgmoth's Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Yawgmoth%27s+Will) to return the [Pithing Needle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pithing+Needle) to play, once again locking the Bazaar out. And once again, Hornung had the [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) to deal with it. Mastriano had made a small mistake with his Will, forgetting to reuse a [Mystical Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mystical+Tutor) in his graveyard, something that would come back to haunt him as Hornung went crazy on him, making a slew of Zombies, which got to take care of business free of a [Chain of Vapor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chain+of+Vapor). The Zombies turned sideways, and handed a sweet looking [Time Walk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Time+Walk) to **Mark Hornung, the 2011 Vintage Champion!**


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/usnat11/vin%20winner.JPG)*Mark Hornung, 2011 Vintage Champion*
